Purport

ÅšrÄ« Caitanya MahÄprabhu was the Supreme Personality of Godhead playing the part of a very great, advanced devotee. On the mahÄ-bhÄgavata platform, the devotee makes no distinction between friends and enemies. On that platform he sees everyone as a servant of Ká¹›á¹£á¹‡a. As stated in the Bhagavad-gÄ«tÄ (5.18):

vidyÄ-vinaya-sampanne brÄhmaá¹‡e gavi hastini
Å›uni caiva Å›va-pÄke ca paá¹‡á¸itÄá¸¥ sama-darÅ›inaá¸¥

â€œThe humble sages, by virtue of true knowledge, see with equal vision a learned and gentle brÄhmaá¹‡a, a cow, an elephant, a dog, and a dog-eater [outcaste].â€

A mahÄ-bhÄgavata, being learned and advanced in spiritual consciousness, sees no difference between a tiger, an elephant or a learned scholar. The test of advanced spiritual consciousness is that one becomes fearless. He envies no one, and he is always engaged in the Lordâ€™s service. He sees every living entity as an eternal part and parcel of the Lord, rendering service according to his capacity by the will of the Supreme Lord. As Ká¹›á¹£á¹‡a confirms in the Bhagavad-gÄ«tÄ (15.15):

*sarvasya cÄhaá¹ há¹›di sanniviá¹£á¹­o * â€ƒmattaá¸¥ smá¹›tir jÃ±Änam apohanaá¹ ca

â€œI am seated in everyoneâ€™s heart, and from Me come remembrance, knowledge and forgetfulness.â€

The mahÄ-bhÄgavata knows that Ká¹›á¹£á¹‡a is in everyoneâ€™s heart. Ká¹›á¹£á¹‡a is dictating, and the living entity is following His dictations. Ká¹›á¹£á¹‡a is within the heart of the tiger, elephant and boar. Therefore Ká¹›á¹£á¹‡a tells them, â€œHere is a mahÄ-bhÄgavata.
